INTRODUCTION
1.1 in my Report on the Provisional Recommendationg which was published on
3 September 1991 I outlined the background to the Review of the Local
Government Boundariea and explained the general criteria and principles
involved. The Report also highlighted my consideration of the main issues
which aroae through the initial comments received from local councils,
political parties, associations, organisations, community groups and
individual members of the public.
PROVISIONAL RECOMMENDATIONS
4.3 The information presented to me was invariably based on extensive local
knowledge and was invaluable in assisting my review of the Provisional
Recommendations. I hope that the extent to which my Provisional
Recommendations have been altered az a result will reassure the public
that the consultative process wag meaningful and that it was worth their
while making their vlews known.
REVISIONS TO THE PROVISIONAL RECOMMENDATIONS

were not required in the following seven districta and I see no need to

## Page 4

In the remaining s@ven districte I have decided to recommend substantial
Revisions to my Provisional Recommendations which are briefly summarised
below:-
Belfast
While I received representations on behalf of Belfast City Councll
that the district boundary be revised to include parts of Lisburn,
Castlereagh and Newtownabbey, and the same issue was raised in
hearinge in Newtownabbey, Lisburn and Castlereagh, I have decided, for the reasons outlined in the Provisional Report, to recommend no change to this boundary.
The following additional iseues arose at the Belfast Hearing.
(i) The unsuitability of the proposed boundary of Island ward which divided Island Street in East Beifast. I have been
able to recommend an alternative line which removea the cause for objection.
(il) The likelihood that the provisionally recommended boundary of Glencairn and Legoniel wards would deter people from voting aCross ‘peace lines’. JY am now recommending the restoration Of the existing boundaries between the Glencairn, Legoniel and Ballysillan wards which should meet these objections.
(iid) The undesirability of creating a ward extending from the Donegall Road to Finaghy in South Belfast, and the unsuitability of some ward boundaries in the Botanic/ Stranmillis area. An extensive review of South Belfast wards enabled me to recommend a redrawing which solves the firat problem. It has also produced a recommendation for a new ward in South Belfast (which I had indicated as dagirable in the Provisional Recommendations} Bringing the total number of wards in Belfast back to 51.
Castlereagh
in order to satisfactorily overcome the Councils unanimous objection to certain ward boundariea substantial Revielons are recommended
which include the creation of an additional ward and the alignment of Ward boundaries along the dual-carriageway.
Arda
At the Hearing additional local knowledge about community identity and related ward boundaries was presented which allowed me to @etablish a District baged on a coherent 23 Ward atructure, within
the guidelines.

I am convinced by the strength of local feeling, and by Ng ilce
confidence that the proposed new district would protect : Pp
character of the area, that I should Revise my Provigsiona ™
Recommendationa on the proposed merger and retain the pie g
external boundaries of Ballymoney, Moyle and Ballymena loca ,
government districts. The internal ward boundary ge irae Ot ce
Ballymoney and Moyle have therefore been revised in Line w is -_
existing ward numbers. The difficulty Of ereqteng wards Ww :
recognised local identities while maintaining the principle : '
equivalent ward electorate has been most pronounced in the G eo *
One of the consequences of retaining Moyle is the need to treat the
Glens as a special geographical area which forces me to depart from '
my agreed tolerance of +10% on the average ward electorate in reapec
of the Glenaan ward.
Internal ward boundaries in Ballymena remain unchanged.
The extent of the individual local government district hevieions are
detailed in the revised district maps published in association with this
Report. No maps are published in respect of the ten districte referred to
above where I have decided not to Revise my provisionally recommended ward
and diatrict boundaries.

5.6 Following receipt of written representationa at this Revised Stage I may,
if I think it advisable, hold further Public Hearings. This would be
justified in my opinion only where new evidence was being produced in the
written gubmissions, and not merely for the rehearsal of arguments which
have already been considered at earlier stages.
= ee A When all representationa in writing have been considered together with any
further oral representations presented, the Final Stage of the Review will
be the submission of a Report to Government outlining my Final
Recommendations, probably in June 1992.
